The actual root cause is now clear: the legacy C++ wrapper headers use pointers to anonymous structs in public function signatures. In C++, those types have no linkage, so any function that mentions them also ends up with no usable external linkage. That explains all three symptoms at once: the old C++ wrappers “compiled” but didn’t export symbols, the shim only exported `CVodeFree(void*)`, and the `SolveIt::CVodeDerivative` callbacks were emitted as non-external. I’m naming the relevant wrapper struct types now so the symbols can actually link across translation units.
